# PRFMR — Mobile Replication Guide

Complete specification for replicating PRFMR in a new Replit project.  
Target: a React Native / Expo mobile app (or a second PWA) that is **functionally identical** to the existing web app.

## 1. App Overview & Vision

PRFMR is a **mobile-first nutrition and training tracker** built for combat athletes (MMA, boxing, wrestling, BJJ) and other high-performance athletes. It sits in the gap between generic calorie counters (MyFitnessPal) and coach-led software — giving a solo athlete the data-driven tools a sports nutritionist would use.

**Core user jobs-to-be-done:**
- Know exactly how many calories and macros to eat today (adjusted for training)
- Log food fast without manual lookup (barcode, quick-add, natural language)
- Understand micronutrient quality, not just macros
- Plan and execute a fight-camp weight cut with daily guidance
- Track training load and avoid overtraining

**Design philosophy:**
- Conservative framing — never over-promise
- Transparent calculations — show the maths
- Dark theme throughout
- Mobile-first layout (max-width ~430px cards, bottom-nav style)
- Space Grotesk for headings, Inter for body text

---

## 2. Technology Stack

### Frontend
| Concern | Choice |
|---|---|
| Framework | React 18 + TypeScript |
| Build tool | Vite |
| Routing | Wouter |
| Server state | TanStack React Query v5 |
| Styling | Tailwind CSS + shadcn/ui (Radix UI) |
| Animation | Framer Motion |
| Charts | Recharts |
| Forms | react-hook-form + zodResolver |
| Icons | lucide-react + react-icons/si |
| Barcode scanner | html5-qrcode |

### Backend
| Concern | Choice |
|---|---|
| Runtime | Node.js + Express (TypeScript, ESM) |
| ORM | Drizzle ORM |
| Database | PostgreSQL |
| Sessions | connect-pg-simple + express-session |
| Auth | Passport.js (local + Google OAuth 2.0) |
| Password hashing | Argon2 |
| Email | Resend |
| File storage | Replit Object Storage |
| Push | web-push (VAPID) |

### Shared
- `shared/schema.ts` — single source of truth for all Drizzle table definitions, Zod insert schemas, and TypeScript types
- `shared/routes.ts` — typed route constants (API path + method, shared between client and server)
- `shared/weight-cut.ts` — pure weight-cut calculation engine (no DB, no Express)
- `shared/utils.ts` — `getMicronutrientValue()` and other helpers

## 3. Database Schema (all tables)

All tables are defined with Drizzle ORM in `shared/schema.ts`.  
Column types: `serial`, `integer`, `real`, `text`, `boolean`, `timestamp`, `jsonb`.

### 3.1 `users_auth` — Authentication records
```
id            serial PK
username      text UNIQUE NOT NULL
email         text UNIQUE
passwordHash  text
googleId      text UNIQUE
displayName   text
emailVerified boolean default false
isAdmin       boolean default false
createdAt     timestamp
```

### 3.2 `users` — Profile + calculated targets
```
id                  serial PK (same id as users_auth)
username            text FK
gender              text  ('male'|'female')
age                 integer
height              integer  (cm)
weight              real     (kg)
activityLevel       text     ('sedentary'|'light'|'moderate'|'active'|'very_active')

experienceLevel     text     ('beginner'|'intermediate'|'advanced')
bodyFatPct          real
targetCalories      integer
targetProtein       integer
targetCarbs         integer
targetFat           integer
profilePhotoUrl     text
fightCampActive     boolean  default false
fightDate           text     (YYYY-MM-DD)
weighInTiming       text     ('same_day'|'day_before')
onboardingComplete  boolean  default false
-- Onboarding survey fields (all text unless noted):
surveyCutExperience
surveyCutOutcome
surveyCalorieKnowledge
```

## 4. Backend Architecture

```
server/
  index.ts              Express app entry — session, passport, route registration, seeding
  auth.ts               Passport.js configuration (local + Google OAuth strategies, requireAuth middleware)
  auth-routes.ts        Mounted at /api/auth — all authentication endpoints
  invite-routes.ts      Mounted at /api/invites — invite request + validation
  feedback-routes.ts    Absolute paths /api/feedback/* — feedback submission + attachments
  routes.ts             All remaining API handlers (~4279 lines)
  storage.ts            IStorage interface + storage singleton export
  database-storage.ts   DrizzleStorage — implements IStorage against PostgreSQL
  db.ts                 Drizzle ORM + PostgreSQL pool setup
  seed-catalogs.ts      On-startup catalog seeder (exercises, activities, supplements, ingredients)
  vite.ts               Vite dev-server integration (development only)
  static.ts             Static file serving (production only)
  lib/
    amqs.ts             AMQS scoring engine
    micros.ts           Micronutrient extraction + COMPOSITE_FOODS map
    energy.ts           Calorie burn helpers — MET formula, RPE adjustment, lifting estimator
    readiness.ts        Session Readiness Score composite
    fuel-availability.ts  Fuel / glycogen pre-session status
    training-load.ts    ACWR, load classification, lifting calorie estimates
    email.ts            Resend email helper (verification, welcome, password reset, invites)
    push-notifications.ts  VAPID web-push helpers
    verification-tokens.ts  Email verification token generation/validation
    password-reset-tokens.ts  Password reset token generation/validation
    version.ts          App version + environment helpers
    beta-cap.ts         Active user count + beta limit helpers
    offMatch.ts         Open Food Facts ingredient auto-matching logic
    searchRanking.ts    Food search ranking/sorting logic
    provisional-readiness.ts  Provisional check-in status logic
    weight-cut.ts       (mirrors shared/weight-cut.ts — server-side import alias)
  replit_integrations/
    object_storage/
      routes.ts         Object storage upload/download routes
      objectStorage.ts  ObjectStorageService class
      objectAcl.ts      ACL helpers for public/private paths

shared/
  schema.ts             All Drizzle tables, Zod insert schemas, TypeScript types
  routes.ts             Typed API route constants
  weight-cut.ts         Pure weight-cut calculation functions
  utils.ts              getMicronutrientValue() and helpers
  username-validation.ts  validateUsername(), normalizeUsername(), RESERVED_USERNAMES

data/
  ingredients.json      307 ingredients with full macro + micro data (see §26)
```

### Route mounting order (server/routes.ts `registerRoutes()`)
```
app.use("/api/auth",    authRoutes)          → auth-routes.ts endpoints
app.use("/api/invites", inviteRoutes)         → invite-routes.ts endpoints
app.use(feedbackRoutes)                       → /api/feedback/* direct paths
registerObjectStorageRoutes(app)              → /api/objects/*
GET /auth/google                             → Google OAuth redirect
GET /auth/google/callback                    → Google OAuth callback
... all remaining /api/* routes from routes.ts
```

### Global middleware
- `express.json()` — parses JSON bodies, stores rawBody on request
- `express.urlencoded({ extended: false })` — URL-encoded bodies
- `setupAuth(app)` — installs session middleware, Passport, local + Google strategies
- All `/api` routes have `Cache-Control: no-store` headers set globally

### Authentication guard (`getAuthenticatedUser`)
Every protected route in `routes.ts` calls this helper first:
```typescript
async function getAuthenticatedUser(req, res): Promise<{ authUser, profileUser } | null>
// Returns null and sends 401/404 if not authenticated or profile not found
// authUser → from usersAuth table (session), profileUser → from users table
```

### Storage interface pattern
All database operations flow through `IStorage` (in `server/storage.ts`).  
Routes call `storage.someMethod(args)` — never raw Drizzle in routes.  
`DrizzleStorage` in `server/database-storage.ts` implements the interface against PostgreSQL.

### `calculateTargets()` — exported from routes.ts
```typescript
calculateTargets({ gender, weight, height, age, activityLevel, goal }): {
  bmr: number,
  tdee: number,
  targetCalories: number,
  targetProtein: number,
  targetFat: number,
  targetCarbs: number,
  trainingCalorieCreditPct: number,
  goal: string,
}
```
Also exported: `TRAINING_CALORIE_CREDIT_PCT = { fat_loss: 0.5, maintenance: 0.75, weight_gain: 1.0, fight_camp: 0.5 }`

---

## 5. Calculation Engine

All core maths lives in `server/routes.ts` `calculateTargets()` and `shared/weight-cut.ts`.

### 5.1 BMR — Mifflin-St Jeor
```
BMR = (10 × weight_kg) + (6.25 × height_cm) − (5 × age)
      + 5   (male)
      − 161 (female)
```

### 5.2 TDEE
```
Multipliers:
  sedentary   × 1.2
  light       × 1.375
  moderate    × 1.55
  active      × 1.725
  very_active × 1.9

TDEE = BMR × multiplier
```

### 5.3 Goal-based calorie targets
| Goal | Calories | Protein | Fat |
|---|---|---|---|
| fat_loss | TDEE − 500 | 2.2 g/kg | 0.7 g/kg |
| maintenance | TDEE | 1.8 g/kg | 0.8 g/kg |
| weight_gain | TDEE + 300 | 1.8 g/kg | 0.9 g/kg |

### 5.4 Dynamic carbs
```
Carbs = (targetCalories − (protein × 4) − (fat × 9)) / 4
```
Carbs are always the residual macro — protein and fat are fixed first.

### 5.5 Training calorie credits
When the user logs a training session, extra calories are added back:
```
Credit pct:
  fat_loss    → 50%
  maintenance → 75%
  weight_gain → 100%

Adjusted target calories = base target + (sessionKcal × creditPct)
```

### 5.6 Fight Camp target override
Priority order (highest wins):
1. **Fight Camp Active** — macro model driven by `weighInTiming` and weeks to fight
2. **Profile Goal** (fat_loss / maintenance / weight_gain)
3. **Maintenance fallback**

Fight camp models:
- `same_day` cut: more aggressive deficit, lower carbs
- `day_before` cut: moderate deficit, carb management before rehydration window

---

## 6. AMQS — Athlete Micronutrient Quality Score

Defined in `server/lib/amqs.ts`. Returns a score 0–100 and tier label.

### 6.1 Tracked nutrients (17 total)

The micro keys used throughout the codebase (in `ingredients.json`, `MICRO_KEYS` array in `micros.ts`, and `supplement_catalog.microsPerUnit`) use the suffix format below. **Use these exact key names** when building the data model.

| DB/JSON key | Display name | L1 Baseline Target | L2 Athlete Target |
|---|---|---|---|
| `vitamin_c_mg` | Vitamin C | 90 mg | 200 mg |
| `vitamin_d_ug` | Vitamin D | 20 mcg | 50 mcg |
| `vitamin_b12_ug` | Vitamin B12 | 2.4 mcg | 4 mcg |
| `vitamin_b6_mg` | Vitamin B6 | 1.7 mg | 3 mg |
| `folate_ug` | Folate | 400 mcg | 600 mcg |
| `vitamin_a_ug` | Vitamin A | 900 mcg | 1200 mcg |
| `vitamin_b2_mg` | Vitamin B2 (Riboflavin) | 1.3 mg | 2 mg |
| `vitamin_b1_mg` | Vitamin B1 (Thiamine) | 1.2 mg | 2 mg |
| `vitamin_b3_mg` | Vitamin B3 (Niacin) | 16 mg | 25 mg |
| `iron_mg` | Iron | 8 mg (M) / 18 mg (F) | 12 mg (M) / 25 mg (F) |
| `calcium_mg` | Calcium | 1000 mg | 1300 mg |
| `magnesium_mg` | Magnesium | 420 mg (M) / 320 mg (F) | 500 mg |
| `zinc_mg` | Zinc | 11 mg (M) / 8 mg (F) | 14 mg (M) / 11 mg (F) |
| `potassium_mg` | Potassium | 3500 mg | 4700 mg |
| `iodine_ug` | Iodine | 150 mcg | 200 mcg |
| `omega3_g` | Omega-3 | 1.1 g | 3 g |
| `selenium_ug` | Selenium | 55 mcg | 70 mcg |

`ingredients.json` stores each micro as `{key}_per_100g` (e.g. `iron_mg_per_100g`). All values are per 100 g of the ingredient (cooked basis where a `cookFactor` applies).

### 6.2 Two-layer scoring model

**L1 — Baseline Adequacy (50% of score)**  
Linear 0→1 as intake moves from 0 → L1 target.

**L2 — Athlete Optimization (50% of score)**  
Linear 0→1 as intake moves from L1 target → L2 target.

Per nutrient: `nutrientScore = (L1score × 0.5) + (L2score × 0.5)`  
Total: `rawScore = average(nutrientScore × weight) × 100`

Nutrient weights vary (critical nutrients get higher weight):
- Critical (iron, calcium, vitD, magnesium, zinc): weight 1.5
- Important (omega3, vitB12, potassium, fibre, vitC): weight 1.2
- Standard: weight 1.0

### 6.3 Elite gate
A score can only reach the "Elite" tier if **all critical nutrients** (iron, calcium, vitD, magnesium, zinc) are at ≥70% of their L1 target.

### 6.4 Tier thresholds
| Score | Tier |
|---|---|
| ≥ 95 | Elite |
| ≥ 85 | Optimal |
| ≥ 70 | Good |
| ≥ 50 | Fair |
| < 50 | Basic |

> **Note on Elite cap:** Even with a score ≥ 95, the tier is downgraded to **Optimal** if any of the six *critical nutrients* (Vitamin D, Magnesium, Zinc, Iron, Omega-3, Calcium) falls below 70% of its Layer-1 target.

### 6.5 Confidence rating
Based on % of food entries that have micronutrient data:
- 0–30%: Low
- 31–60%: Medium
- 61–100%: High

### 6.6 Supplement micros → AMQS connection (full frontend spec)

#### How supplements feed the score
Supplement intakes for the day are aggregated server-side and added to food micronutrient totals before AMQS scoring. Formula: `microsPerUnit × doseAmount` from `supplement_catalog.microsPerUnit`. Only intakes marked `taken === true` on that date count. Only catalog-linked supplements (non-null `catalogId`) contribute — custom supplements with no catalog link contribute zero.

The merged total is served by `GET /api/me/amqs/micros/:date` and is what the server uses when computing `GET /api/me/amqs/score/:date`.

#### What the AMQS score API returns (supplement-relevant fields)
```typescript
// GET /api/me/amqs/score/:date response
{
  score: number
  tier: string
  confidence: "Low" | "Medium" | "High"
  totals: Record<string, number>       // combined food + supplement intake per nutrient
  breakdown: {
    food:        Record<string, number> // food-only intake per nutrient
    supplements: Record<string, number> // supplement-only intake per nutrient
  }
  coverageStats: {
    totalTakenSupplements?: number      // # of supplements marked taken today
  }
  topGaps: { microKey, label, pctOfTarget, suggestion? }[]
  allMet: boolean
  // ... layer2 fields
}
```

#### Frontend signals driven by supplement data

**1. Empty state gate (AMQSCard)**
The card shows data (not the empty/provisional state) when either:
- `daily.confidence !== "Low"` AND `daily.score > 0` (`hasFoodToday`), **OR**
- `daily.coverageStats?.totalTakenSupplements > 0` (`hasSupplementsToday`)

This means: **if a user has taken supplements but logged no food**, the AMQS card still exits the empty state and shows a real score.

**2. "What moved it" subtitle (AMQSCard)**
This one-line summary on the main card is computed from `daily.breakdown`:
```
combined = { ...breakdown.food } merged with { ...breakdown.supplements }
topEntry = highest-value nutrient across the combined map
```
Output format: `"+{value}% {NutrientLabel} · {gap.label} at {pct}%"`

A supplement micro (e.g. Vitamin D from a Vitamin D3 supplement) will appear as the top contributor if it is the largest nutrient value in the combined breakdown — the card does not distinguish food vs supplement in this text.

**3. "AMQS tracked" badge on supplement shelf**
Any supplement with a non-null `catalogId` shows:
- `<Badge variant="default" className="text-[10px]">AMQS tracked</Badge>`
- Sub-line: `<p className="text-xs text-muted-foreground/60 mt-0.5">Contributing to your AMQS score</p>`

Important nuance: supplements with a `catalogId` but an empty `microsPerUnit: {}` (e.g. Creatine, Vitamin K2) still show the "AMQS tracked" badge, but they contribute zero micros to the score. The badge means "linked to catalog", not necessarily "moves the score".

**4. Cache invalidation on supplement mutations**
Any add, edit, or delete of a supplement immediately invalidates:
```
["/api/me/amqs/score"]        (exact: false — all date variants)
["/api/me/amqs/score-range"]  (exact: false — all range variants)
```
This ensures the AMQS card refreshes as soon as a supplement is saved or removed.

**5. Baseline completion — three related UI elements**

When all Layer-1 targets are met (`daily.allMet === true`), three separate UI elements respond. These are independent — replicate all three.

**5a. One-time toast**

Triggered by a `useEffect` watching `[daily?.allMet, date]`:

```typescript
useEffect(() => {
  if (!daily || !daily.allMet) return;
  const key = `amqs-l1-complete-${date}`;           // date = "YYYY-MM-DD"
  if (localStorage.getItem(key)) return;             // already fired today — skip
  localStorage.setItem(key, "1");                    // mark as fired
  toast({
    title: "Baseline adequacy covered",
    description: "All key micronutrient targets met today. Now optimise for athlete targets.",
    duration: 5000,
  });
}, [daily?.allMet, date]);
```

Key rules:
- The localStorage key is `amqs-l1-complete-{date}` (e.g. `amqs-l1-complete-2026-06-21`). A new key is created per calendar day so the toast re-fires on a new day if the user hits the target again.
- The toast fires at most once per day, even if the component re-renders or the user navigates away and back.
- The `date` prop comes from the dashboard's `selectedDate` state — it is the date currently in view, not necessarily today.
- The toast uses the standard `useToast` hook (shadcn `Toaster`). No custom variant — it renders as a default toast.

**5b. Inline card callout (replaces top-gaps list)**

When `daily.allMet === true`, the "Top gaps" section at the bottom of the main AMQS card is **replaced** by this green callout:

```
data-testid="amqs-all-met"
className="pt-3"

Inner div: "flex items-center gap-2 p-3 rounded-lg bg-emerald-500/10 border border-emerald-500/20"
  <ShieldCheck className="h-4 w-4 text-emerald-500 shrink-0" />
  <p className="text-xs text-emerald-600 dark:text-emerald-400 font-medium leading-tight">
    Baseline adequacy covered. Tap to see athlete optimisation targets.
  </p>
```

This callout is shown instead of the `topGaps` bars. The card remains tappable (opens the detail dialog) so the user can view Layer-2 athlete targets.

**5c. Detail dialog callout (score ≥ 85, not strictly tied to allMet)**

Inside the AMQS detail dialog, when `daily.score >= 85`, a separate green callout appears above the gaps lists:

```
data-testid="callout-layer1-strong"
className="flex items-start gap-2 p-3 rounded-lg bg-emerald-500/10 border border-emerald-500/20"

  <ShieldCheck className="h-4 w-4 text-emerald-500 shrink-0 mt-0.5" />
  <p className="text-xs text-emerald-600 dark:text-emerald-400 leading-relaxed">
    Baseline micronutrient needs covered. If you're training hard, consider optimising
    toward athlete targets.
  </p>
```

Note: this triggers at `score >= 85`, not at `allMet`. A user can have `allMet === true` with a score below 85 (or vice versa) — they are independent conditions. Both can be visible simultaneously inside the dialog.

**6. AMQS detail dialog footer disclaimer**
The detail dialog (opened by tapping the AMQS card) always shows at the bottom:
```
"Based on logged foods and supplements. Estimates only; not medical advice."
```

---

## 7. Session Readiness Score

Defined in `server/lib/readiness.ts`. Composite score 0–100 from 4 components.

| Component | Max Points | Logic |
|---|---|---|
| Sleep | 30 | < 5h = 0; 5–6h = 15; 6–7h = 20; 7–8h = 25; ≥ 8h = 30. Sleep quality (1–5) adds up to 5 bonus pts. |
| Energy Availability | 30 | Based on yesterday's calorie intake vs target. At/above target = 30; 75–99% = 22; 50–74% = 12; <50% = 4 |
| Carb Sufficiency | 25 | Based on yesterday's carb intake vs target. ≥100% = 25; 75–99% = 18; 50–74% = 10; <50% = 3 |
| AMQS | 15 | Elite=15; Optimal=12; Good=9; Fair=5; Basic=2 |

**Labels:**
- ≥ 85 → High
- ≥ 70 → Moderate
- ≥ 55 → Low
- < 55 → Poor
- **Provisional** — if sleep or yesterday food data is missing

If data is missing, a **Provisional Check-In** card is shown on the dashboard so the user can self-report (feel: fresh/okay/tired; fueled: yes/somewhat/no; planned intensity: light/moderate/hard).

---

## 8. Fuel Availability & Glycogen Risk

Defined in `server/lib/fuel-availability.ts`. Returns a status label + supporting numbers.

Inputs used:
- Yesterday's carb intake
- Today's training plan (expected kcal burn + intensity)
- User's weight (for glycogen capacity estimates)
- Whether today is a rest day

Status labels (in descending priority):
1. **REST_DAY** — user marked today as rest
2. **NO_TRAINING** — no session logged/planned
3. **WELL_FUELLED** — carbs + reserves sufficient for planned training
4. **MODERATE_RISK** — carbs low, performance may suffer
5. **HIGH_RISK** — significant glycogen deficit, high injury/fatigue risk
6. **DEPLETED** — severely under-fuelled for the planned load

The calculation compares yesterday's carb intake against a threshold based on body weight (≈3–5 g/kg depending on intensity) minus the expected carb cost of today's session.

---

## 9. Weight-Cut Engine

Defined in `shared/weight-cut.ts` — **pure functions, no side effects**.

### 9.1 Two flows: `same_day` vs `day_before`

**same_day** — athlete competes on the same day as weigh-in:
- All weight loss must come from sustainable fat loss (1% BW/week cap)
- No water manipulation window available
- Harder: requires longer run-up

**day_before** — athlete weighs in the day before competing:
- Allows temporary water/glycogen reduction in the final 24–48h
- Fat loss component handles the structural deficit
- Temp cut component handles the final flush

### 9.2 `calculateWeightCutPlan(inputs)` — main entry point

Inputs:
```typescript
{
  currentWeight: number   // kg
  targetWeight: number    // kg
  fightDate: string       // YYYY-MM-DD
  weighInTiming: 'same_day' | 'day_before'
  manualTempReductionKg?: number  // override auto-calc of water cut portion
}
```

Returns:
```typescript
{
  totalDrop: number             // kg to lose
  fatLossDrop: number           // kg via fat loss
  tempCutDrop: number           // kg via water/glycogen (day_before only)
  weeksAvailable: number
  recommendedWeeklyRate: number // kg/week fat loss
  isAchievable: boolean
  status: CutStatus  // 'on_track'|'aggressive'|'very_aggressive'|'unrealistic'|'complete'|'past_date'
  weeklyTargets: WeeklyTarget[] // for chart
  warnings: string[]
}
```

### 9.3 `buildWeeklyTargets()`

Produces an array of `{ week, projectedWeight, caloricDeficitPerDay }` for the weight trend chart on the dashboard and in ShareMomentSheet.

### 9.4 Constraints
  - Max sustainable fat loss: 1% of body weight per week (hard cap)
  - Temp cut capped at 5–8% body weight (adjustable by `manualTempReductionKg`)
  - Risk/status is driven by `requiredWeeklyRatePct` — the % of current bodyweight that must be lost per week to reach target in time. It is **not** an absolute kg threshold (a 90 kg athlete has a higher cap than a 55 kg one):

  | requiredWeeklyRatePct | CutStatus | Label shown to user |
  |---|---|---|
  | ≤ 0.5% BW/wk | `on_track` | "Steady pace" |
  | ≤ 1.0% BW/wk | `on_track` | "On track" |
  | ≤ 1.5% BW/wk | `aggressive` | "Quite aggressive — consider extending timeline" |
  | ≤ 2.0% BW/wk | `very_aggressive` | "Very aggressive — adjust target or date" |
  | > 2.0% BW/wk | `unrealistic` | "Unrealistic — not achievable safely" |

  **Pace badge** on `WeightCutHero` uses the *recommended* rate (capped at 1% BW/wk via `getPaceInfo(weeklyRatePct)`):
  - < 0.5% → "Easy pace" (muted grey)
  - ≤ 0.75% → "Moderate pace" (orange)
  - > 0.75% → "Aggressive pace" (yellow)

  Full `CutStatus` type: `"on_track" | "aggressive" | "very_aggressive" | "unrealistic" | "complete" | "past_date"`

---

## 10. Training Log & Load System

### 10.1 Calorie burn estimation
Defined in `server/lib/energy.ts`.

#### Core MET formula (`kcalFromMET`)
```
kcal/min = MET × 3.5 × bodyWeightKg / 200
sessionKcal = kcal/min × durationMinutes
```
Returns 0 if any input is zero or negative.

#### Strength training METs (`getStrengthMET`)
Used when no MET value comes from the activity catalog:
```
light    → 3.5
moderate → 5.0  ← default when intensity is null/unknown
vigorous → 6.0
```

#### Session calorie calculator (`calculateSessionCalories`)
```typescript
calculateSessionCalories(
  weightKg: number,
  input: {
    durationMinutes?: number | null,
    intensity?: string | null,
    sets?: Array<{ restSeconds?: number | null }>,
    activities?: Array<{ metValue: number; durationMinutes: number }>
  }
): { totalKcal, strengthKcal, activityKcal, estimatedMinutes }
```
- If `durationMinutes` is not provided but `sets` are, duration is **estimated from sets** (see below)
- Strength kcal = `kcalFromMET(strengthMET, weight, strengthMinutes)`
- Activity/cardio kcal = sum of `kcalFromMET(activity.metValue, weight, activity.durationMinutes)` for each activity
- `totalKcal = strengthKcal + activityKcal` (rounded)

#### Duration estimation from sets (`estimateDurationFromSets`)
When `durationMinutes` is absent and sets are available:
```
avgRestSeconds = mean of provided restSeconds values,
                 or 90s default if none provided
totalSeconds   = setCount × (35s per set + avgRestSeconds)
estimatedMinutes = ceil(totalSeconds / 60)
```
Default timing constants:
- `avgSetTimeSeconds = 35`
- `defaultRestSeconds = 90`

#### RPE adjustment for cardio (`getRpeKcalAdjustmentFactor`)
Applied **only to cardio** activities when the user logs an RPE value:
```
factor = 0.9 + (clamp(rpe, 1, 10) / 10) × 0.2
  RPE 1  → ×0.92
  RPE 5  → ×1.00
  RPE 10 → ×1.10
finalKcal = baseKcal × factor
```
**Not applied to lifting** — lifting uses `estimateLiftingCalories()` which has its own RPE model.  
**Not applied to leisure/recovery activities** — these are excluded by name:

```
Excluded keywords (if activity name contains any of these, no RPE adjustment):
"leisure", "easy", "recovery", "warmup", "warm-up", "warm up",
"cooldown", "cool-down", "cool down", "mobility", "stretch",
"stretching", "gentle", "casual", "walking", "walk"
```

`shouldApplyRpeKcalAdjustment(activityName, activityType)` returns `false` for `activityType === "lifting"` or any name matching the exclusion list.

#### Lifting calorie estimation (`estimateLiftingCalories`)
Separate model used for `activityType === "lifting"` entries in `session_activities`:
```typescript
estimateLiftingCalories({
  bodyRegion: 'upper' | 'lower' | 'full',
  durationMinutes: number,
  rpe: number,       // 1–10
  bodyWeightKg: number
}): number
```
METs by body region:
```
lower → 5.5
full  → 5.0
upper → 4.5
```
RPE is baked into this model directly (not via the cardio RPE factor).

#### kcal-per-rep display (`estimateKcalPerRep`)
```typescript
estimateKcalPerRep(totalKcal: number, totalReps: number): number | null
// Returns null if either input is 0; otherwise rounds to 1 decimal
// Purely a rough reference for the user — not medically accurate
```

### 10.2 Training Load System — complete specification

Source file: `server/lib/training-load.ts`

This system turns raw training data (RPE, duration, body region) into a daily load score, classifies it against a personalised baseline, generates natural-language warnings, and surfaces them both as an inline card on the training page and as a modal dialog.

---

#### 10.2.1 Per-activity load score — `computeSessionLoad()`

Every activity in a session contributes a load score:

```
if rpe is present:
  activityLoad = rpe × durationMinutes

else (no RPE — e.g. machine cardio with auto-kcal):
  activityLoad = estimatedKcal  (used as a proxy)
```

A session's contribution is the **sum** of all its activities' load scores.

**Lifting-specific load (for display on activity card, not used in ACWR):**
```
trainingLoadScore = durationMinutes × sessionRpe × bodyRegionMultiplier

bodyRegionMultiplier:
  upper → 1.0
  lower → 1.25
  full  → 1.1
```

---

#### 10.2.2 Day total — `computeDailyLoad()`

Sums `computeSessionLoad()` across all activities for the day.

```typescript
{
  totalLoad:            number      // sum of all activity load scores
  classification:       DayClassification
  provisional:          boolean     // true if it's still today (partial data) or sessions exist but no activities
  sessionCount:         number
  totalDurationMinutes: number
  totalKcal:            number
}
```

**Day classification thresholds — `classifyDayLoad()`**

| `totalLoad` (RPE × minutes) | Classification |
|---|---|
| < 300 | `"light"` |
| 300–599 | `"moderate"` |
| 600–899 | `"hard"` |
| ≥ 900 | `"very_hard"` |

---

#### 10.2.3 ACWR + warning engine — `computeLoadWarnings()`

Takes today's `DailyLoadResult` and an array of prior days (newest-first).

**Step 1 — Acute load (last 7 days)**
```
acuteLoad  = Σ totalLoad for [today, yesterday, …, 6 days ago]
acuteDaily = Math.round((acuteLoad / 7) × 10) / 10
```

**Step 2 — Active day count**
```
activeDaysInWindow = count of days where totalLoad > 0 across all days in the window
insufficientHistory = activeDaysInWindow < 7
```
When `insufficientHistory` is `true`, ACWR and `relativeLoad` are **both forced to `null`** — a baseline built mostly from zero-load rest days would produce spurious high ratios for new users.

**Step 3 — Baseline (28 → 14 → 7 fallback chain)**
```
for n in [28, 14, 7]:
  if totalDaysAvailable >= n:
    baselineLoad    = Math.round((Σ totalLoad[0..n] / n) × 10) / 10
    baselineDaysUsed = n
    break
```

**Step 4 — ACWR**
```
if !insufficientHistory AND baselineLoad > 0:
  acwr = Math.round((acuteDaily / baselineLoad) × 100) / 100
else:
  acwr = null
```

**Step 5 — Relative load (today vs baseline)**
```
if !insufficientHistory AND baselineLoad > 0:
  relativeLoad = Math.round((todayLoad / baselineLoad) × 100) / 100
else:
  relativeLoad = null
```

**Step 6 — Stress flags**

Per-day high-stress determination (`isHighStress()`):
```
if relativeLoad is not null:  high = relativeLoad > 1.2
else (no baseline):           high = totalLoad >= 600
```

Very-high stress:
```
if relativeLoad is not null:  veryHigh = relativeLoad > 1.4
else:                         veryHigh = totalLoad >= 900
```

Stacking flags (uses today, yesterday, and 2-days-ago):
```
backToBackHardDays = todayHigh AND y1High
highLoadCluster    = 2+ of [today, y1, y2] are high-stress
threeDayStreak     = todayHigh AND y1High AND y2High
```

**Step 7 — loadStatus**
```
if acwr === null:  loadStatus = null
elif acwr < 0.8:  loadStatus = "low"
elif acwr <= 1.5: loadStatus = "stable"
else:             loadStatus = "spike"
```

**Step 8 — Warning text generation**

Up to 2 warnings are generated. Priority order: spike/elevated first, stacking second.

```
Condition                        Warning text
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
acwr > 1.5                       "Today's load is well above your recent baseline.
                                  Consider keeping the next session lighter or
                                  prioritising recovery."

relativeLoad > 1.3               "Today's load is above your recent baseline.
(and acwr ≤ 1.5 or acwr null)    A lighter follow-up session or extra recovery
                                  may help."

threeDayStreak = true            "Training stress has been building across the
                                  last 3 days. It may help to reduce intensity
                                  or include a lighter day."

highLoadCluster = true           "Training stress is accumulating across recent
(and not threeDayStreak)         days. Recovery needs may be higher than usual
                                  over the next 24–48 hours."
```

Final list is capped at `warnings.slice(0, 2)`.

---

#### 10.2.4 ACWR risk bands (displayed in `/load-trend`)

| ACWR value | Label | UI colour |
|---|---|---|
| `null` | "No baseline yet" | `text-muted-foreground` |
| < 0.8 | "Under-trained (< 0.8)" | `text-blue-400` |
| 0.8–1.3 | "Optimal zone (0.8–1.3)" | `text-green-400` |
| 1.3–1.5 | "Elevated risk (1.3–1.5)" | `text-yellow-400` |
| > 1.5 | "High risk spike (> 1.5)" | `text-red-400` |

---

#### 10.2.5 `LoadWarningResult` — full returned shape

```typescript
{
  warnings:            string[]         // 0–2 natural-language warning strings
  backToBackHardDays:  boolean
  highLoadCluster:     boolean
  threeDayStreak:      boolean
  acuteLoad:           number           // 7-day sum
  acuteDaily:          number           // acuteLoad / 7 (1dp)
  baselineLoad:        number | null
  baselineDaysUsed:    number | null    // 28, 14, or 7
  acwr:                number | null
  relativeLoad:        number | null    // today / baseline
  highStress:          boolean
  veryHighStress:      boolean
  chronicLoad:         number           // legacy alias for baselineLoad (0 when null)
  loadRatio:           number | null    // alias for acwr
  loadStatus:          "low"|"stable"|"spike"|null
  activeDaysInWindow:  number
  insufficientHistory: boolean
}
```

---

#### 10.2.6 `GET /api/me/training-load/:date` — full response shape

Auth required. Fetches 28 days of history, applies any user override, then runs `computeLoadWarnings()`.

**Override logic:**
- If the user has saved an override for today (`light` or `moderate`), stress flags (`highStress`, `veryHighStress`) are forced false and stress-related warnings are stripped.
- Overrides for prior days are also respected — `light`/`moderate` prior-day overrides feed corrected classifications back into stacking detection.

```typescript
{
  // From DailyLoadResult (today):
  totalLoad:             number
  classification:        "light"|"moderate"|"hard"|"very_hard"
  provisional:           boolean
  sessionCount:          number
  totalDurationMinutes:  number
  totalKcal:             number

  // Added by the route:
  date:                  string   // "YYYY-MM-DD"
  overrideClassification: string | null
  effectiveClassification: "light"|"moderate"|"hard"|"very_hard"  // override ?? classification

  // From LoadWarningResult (spread in):
  warnings:              string[]
  backToBackHardDays:    boolean
  highLoadCluster:       boolean
  threeDayStreak:        boolean
  acuteLoad:             number
  acuteDaily:            number
  baselineLoad:          number | null
  baselineDaysUsed:      number | null
  acwr:                  number | null
  relativeLoad:          number | null
  highStress:            boolean
  veryHighStress:        boolean
  loadStatus:            "low"|"stable"|"spike"|null
  activeDaysInWindow:    number
  insufficientHistory:   boolean
}
```

---

#### 10.2.7 `GET /api/me/training/load-history/:date` — 28-day chart data

Auth required. Returns history in **chronological order** (oldest first) for chart rendering.

```typescript
{
  history: Array<{
    date:           string   // "YYYY-MM-DD"
    totalLoad:      number
    classification: "light"|"moderate"|"hard"|"very_hard"
    relativeLoad:   number | null   // day totalLoad / baselineLoad (null before 7 active days)
    sessionCount:   number
  }>,
  baselineLoad:      number | null
  baselineDaysUsed:  number | null
  acuteLoad:         number
  acuteDaily:        number
  acwr:              number | null
  date:              string   // the reference date used
}
```

---

#### 10.2.8 `POST /api/me/training/load-override/:date` — save user classification

Auth required. Validated values: `"light"` | `"moderate"` | `"hard"` | `"very_hard"`.

```
Request:  { classification: string }
Response: { success: true, overrideClassification: string }
Error:    400 { message: "Invalid classification" }
```

The override is upserted in `training_load_overrides` table. On the next call to `GET /api/me/training-load/:date`, the `effectiveClassification` reflects it and stress warnings are conditionally suppressed.

---

#### 10.2.9 Frontend — inline load insight on the Training page

The training page (`client/src/pages/training.tsx`) fetches load data on every date change:

```typescript
useQuery({
  queryKey: ["/api/me/training-load", selectedDate],
  queryFn: () => fetch(`/api/me/training-load/${selectedDate}`),
  staleTime: 0,   // always re-fetch on mount
})
```

**`dayLoad` useMemo derivation** — determines the badge shown on the training date card:

1. If `trainingLoadData.effectiveClassification` is present → use it (respects overrides)
2. Otherwise fallback: compute locally from `sessions.activities` using the same thresholds

Badge colour mapping:
```
light       bg-blue-500/15 text-blue-400 border-blue-500/30
moderate    bg-yellow-500/15 text-yellow-400 border-yellow-500/30
hard        bg-orange-500/15 text-orange-400 border-orange-500/30
very_hard   bg-red-500/15 text-red-400 border-red-500/30
```

If the classification was user-overridden, an `(overridden)` note appears next to the badge.

**Inline warning banners:** When `trainingLoadData.warnings` has entries, each is shown below the classification badge as a small `text-orange-400/70` line with an `AlertTriangle` icon (`data-testid="text-load-warning-{i}"`).

**"28-day trend" link:** Always visible below the warnings. Navigates to `/load-trend`. `data-testid="button-view-load-trend"`.

---

#### 10.2.10 Frontend — `checkAndShowLoadWarning()`

Called automatically after every successful mutation that changes training data:
- After adding a lifting set (`addSetMutation.onSuccess`)
- After adding a cardio/activity (`addActivityMutation.onSuccess`)
- After editing an activity (`editActivityMutation.onSuccess`)

```typescript
async function checkAndShowLoadWarning(date: string) {
  const data = await fetch(`/api/me/training-load/${date}`)
  if (data.warnings.length > 0) {
    _pendingLoadWarning = { analysis: data, date }
    setLoadWarningModal({ open: true, analysis: data })
  }
}
```

**`_pendingLoadWarning` — module-level persistence:**  
Declared at module scope (outside the component), not in React state. This means it survives component unmounts (e.g. navigating away to the trend page and back). On component mount, the `useState` initialiser checks `_pendingLoadWarning` for today's date and re-opens the modal if it hasn't been acknowledged yet.

---

#### 10.2.11 Frontend — `TrainingLoadWarningModal`

Component: `client/src/components/TrainingLoadWarningModal.tsx`  
`data-testid="modal-load-warning"`

**Trigger:** Shown when `loadWarningModal.open === true` (set by `checkAndShowLoadWarning`).

**Cannot be dismissed** by clicking outside or pressing Escape — `onInteractOutside` and `onEscapeKeyDown` both call `e.preventDefault()`. The only way to close it is the "Continue" button.

**Layout — three sections:**

1. **Metrics row** (3 equal columns):
   - Today — `analysis.totalLoad` / "load pts"
   - Baseline — `Math.round(analysis.baselineLoad)` / `{N}d avg` (or `"< 7 days"` if null)
   - ACWR — `analysis.acwr.toFixed(2)` / "ratio" (or `"building baseline"` when `insufficientHistory`)

2. **Sparse history notice** (shown only when `analysis.insufficientHistory === true`):
   > "We're still building your training baseline. Until you have at least 7 training days logged, load insights use simple thresholds."

3. **System estimate badge** — `effectiveClassification` displayed with colour coding:
   ```
   light       bg-green-500/20 text-green-400 border-green-500/30
   moderate    bg-yellow-500/20 text-yellow-400 border-yellow-500/30
   hard        bg-orange-500/20 text-orange-400 border-orange-500/30
   very_hard   bg-red-500/20 text-red-400 border-red-500/30
   ```

4. **Warning list** — each warning in a `bg-yellow-500/5 border-yellow-500/20` container. Icon logic:
   - Warning text contains "spike" → `TrendingUp` in `text-red-400`
   - Warning text contains "elevated" → `TrendingUp` in `text-orange-400`
   - Otherwise → `AlertTriangle` in `text-yellow-400`
   - `data-testid="load-warning-{i}"`

5. **Override select** (`data-testid="select-load-override"`):
   ```
   Options:  "Use system estimate" (value="keep") | "Light day" | "Moderate day" | "Hard day" | "Very hard day"
   ```
   When a non-`keep` value is selected, a hint appears: *"Your rating will be saved for this day and used to reduce unnecessary warnings."*

6. **No-baseline notice** (when `analysis.baselineLoad === null`):
   > "You have fewer than 7 days of data. Thresholds are based on absolute load until your baseline is established."

**Actions:**

- **"Continue"** (`data-testid="button-load-acknowledge"`) — if an override was chosen, calls `POST /api/me/training/load-override/{date}` first, then clears `_pendingLoadWarning` and closes the modal.
- **"View 28-day load trend"** (`data-testid="button-view-load-trend"`) — navigates to `/load-trend` **without** closing or acknowledging the modal. The modal re-opens when the user navigates back because `_pendingLoadWarning` is still set.

---

#### 10.2.12 Frontend — Load Trend page (`/load-trend`)

Route: `client/src/pages/load-trend.tsx`  
Data: `GET /api/me/training/load-history/{today}`

**4 summary stat cards:**

| Card label | Value | Sub-label |
|---|---|---|
| ACWR | `data.acwr.toFixed(2)` or `"—"` | ACWR status label (see §10.2.4) |
| Baseline | `Math.round(data.baselineLoad)` or `"—"` | `"{N}-day avg"` or `"< 7 days data"` |
| Acute (7d) | `data.acuteLoad` | `"{data.acuteDaily.toFixed(0)}/day avg"` |
| High-stress | count of days where `relativeLoad > 1.2` (or `totalLoad >= 600` if no baseline) | `"of {trainingDays} training days"` |

**Chart 1 — Absolute Load** (always shown):
- Type: `ComposedChart` with a single `Bar` series (`dataKey="totalLoad"`)
- X-axis: `date`, formatted `"d MMM"`, tick interval 6
- Y-axis: raw load units
- Reference lines (dashed):
  - `y=300` — green `#22c55e` (light/moderate boundary)
  - `y=600` — orange `#f97316` (moderate/hard boundary)
  - `y=900` — red `#ef4444` (hard/very_hard boundary)
  - `y=baselineLoad` — primary colour, labelled `"baseline"` (only when baselineLoad is set)
- Bar fill: `hsl(var(--primary))` at `opacity=0.75`, corner radius `[2,2,0,0]`

**Chart 2 — Relative Load** (only shown when at least one entry has `relativeLoad !== null`):
- Type: `ComposedChart` with a single `Bar` series (`dataKey="relativeLoad"`)
- Y-axis: formatted with `×` suffix
- Reference lines:
  - `y=1.0` — muted, dashed (baseline = 1)
  - `y=1.2` — yellow `#eab308`, labelled `"high stress"`
  - `y=1.4` — red `#ef4444`, labelled `"very high"`
- Sub-note: *"1.0 = exactly at baseline · >1.2 high stress · >1.4 very high stress"*

**Custom tooltip** — shown on bar hover:
```
Date (formatted "EEE d MMM")
Load      {totalLoad}
Relative  {relativeLoad.toFixed(2)}×   (if not null)
Class     {classification}             (coloured)
Sessions  {sessionCount}               (if > 0)
```

**ACWR education card** (always at the bottom):
> "The Acute:Chronic Workload Ratio (ACWR) compares your 7-day average load to your baseline. Research suggests the 'sweet spot' is **0.8–1.3** — below this suggests detraining, above 1.5 indicates injury risk elevation."
> "Baseline window: 28 days → 14 days → 7 days as your history builds."
> Citation: *Gabbett, T.J. (2016). British Journal of Sports Medicine, 50(5), 273–280.*

---

#### 10.2.13 Classification colour reference (all UI contexts)

| Classification | Badge text | Bar colour | Badge CSS classes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `light` | Light | `#22c55e` | `bg-green-500/20 text-green-400` |
| `moderate` | Moderate | `#eab308` | `bg-yellow-500/20 text-yellow-400` |
| `hard` | Hard | `#f97316` | `bg-orange-500/20 text-orange-400` |
| `very_hard` | Very Hard | `#ef4444` | `bg-red-500/20 text-red-400` |

Note: the training page day-badge uses slightly different opacity variants (`/15` background, `/30` border) while the modal uses `/20` background, `/30` border.

## 11. Food Logging System

### 11.1 Entry sources
1. **Manual** — user types macros directly
2. **Core Foods Quick-Add** — pre-curated list of common meals (see §12)
3. **Open Food Facts search** — barcode or text search via `/api/foods/search`
4. **Barcode scan** — html5-qrcode → `/api/food/barcode/:code`
5. **Saved Meals (templates)** — one-tap log of a saved meal template
6. **Copy from another day** — `/api/me/meals/copy`
7. **AI Quick Log** — natural language → `AILogDialog.tsx`

### 11.2 Raw vs cooked weight
Each entry has `enteredBasis: 'raw'|'cooked'` and `isRawWeight: boolean`.  
The server applies a **cook-factor conversion** to standardise all entries to cooked weight before calculating macros/micros.  
Typical factors (stored in `ingredients.json`): rice raw→cooked ≈ 0.4, chicken raw→cooked ≈ 0.75.

### 11.3 Micronutrient resolution chain

`getFoodMicrosForDate()` in `server/lib/micros.ts` processes each food entry in this priority order:

**Step 1 — Composite food name match (highest priority)**  
Check `entry.name.toLowerCase().trim()` against the `COMPOSITE_FOODS` map (see §13).  
If matched:
- Scale each component's gram weight by `loggedGrams / referenceServing`
- Look up each component in `ingredients.json` by case-insensitive name
- Sum `(micro_per_100g × componentGrams) / 100` for each of the 17 `MICRO_KEYS`
- This path is followed for **all** core food quick-add entries

**Step 2 — OFF entry with ingredient mapping**  
If `entry.sourceType === "off"` AND `entry.microSource === "ingredient"` AND `entry.ingredientIndex` is a valid number:
- Look up `ingredients[ingredientIndex]` directly (by array position, not name)
- Sum `(micro_per_100g × entryGrams) / 100`
- This path is followed when the user has mapped a scanned barcode to an ingredient

**Step 3 — Manual entry name fallback**  
If `entry.sourceType !== "off"`:
- Case-insensitive name search in `ingredients.json` (`i.name.toLowerCase() === entry.name.toLowerCase()`)
- If matched, use that ingredient's micros
- Allows whole-food manual entries (e.g. "Chicken breast") to get micros automatically

**Step 4 — No micros**  
OFF entries without a valid mapping (`microSource !== "ingredient"`) are skipped entirely — they contribute zero to AMQS.

#### Micro key lookup helper (`getMicronutrientValue`)
```typescript
// From shared/utils.ts
getMicronutrientValue(ingredient, `${key}_per_100g`)
// Returns null if the key doesn't exist on the ingredient object
```

#### How core foods map to scanned/OFF foods
Core food quick-adds work via **name-based composite matching** (Step 1 above) — no `ingredientIndex` is needed.  
When a user scans a barcode for a product that is similar to a core food (e.g., a branded porridge), the barcode flow runs separately and the user can map it to an ingredient via `/api/food/barcode/:code/map`. The mapping writes `ingredientIndex` and `microSource: "ingredient"` to the `food_entries` row, enabling Step 2 on future lookups.

### 11.4 Barcode flow
1. Client sends barcode to `/api/food/barcode/:code`
2. Server checks `off_product_mappings` for existing mapping
3. If not found → fetches from Open Food Facts API
4. If found with high-confidence match → returns ingredient micros automatically
5. If low confidence → client shows "map to ingredient" UI for the user to pick
6. User selection saved via `/api/food/barcode/:code/map`

### 11.5 Meal sections
Meals: `breakfast`, `lunch`, `dinner`, `snack`  
Snacks are numbered with `snackIndex` (0, 1, 2…) to support multiple snack slots.

### 11.6 Macro warnings
Visual warnings appear when logged macros exceed targets by >10%.

---

## 13. Composite Food Micronutrient Map

Defined in `server/lib/micros.ts` as `COMPOSITE_FOODS`.

**How it works:**
1. The entry name is lowercased and trimmed, then matched as a key in this map
2. Each component references an ingredient by **exact name** in `ingredients.json` (case-insensitive match)
3. Component gram weights are **per reference serving** — they are scaled proportionally if the user logged a different gram amount: `componentGrams × (loggedGrams / referenceServing)`
4. Only ingredients that have tracked micros contribute — coffee/espresso is **intentionally omitted** from all coffee drinks because it contains negligible amounts of the 17 tracked nutrients

> ⚠️ The ingredient names below are the exact strings that must exist in `ingredients.json`. If you rename any ingredient, the composite lookup silently fails (a `validateCompositeIngredients()` startup check warns in console if any are missing).

| Core Food (matched lowercase) | Ref. Serving | Components (ingredient name in ingredients.json → grams) |
|---|---|---|
| porridge (oats + milk) | 250 g | `Oats (Raw)` → 40 g · `Milk (Whole)` → 200 g |
| porridge (oats + water) | 250 g | `Oats (Raw)` → 45 g |
| cappuccino (whole milk) | 240 g | `Milk (Whole)` → 120 g *(espresso omitted — no tracked micros)* |
| latte (whole milk) | 350 g | `Milk (Whole)` → 200 g |
| flat white | 200 g | `Milk (Whole)` → 130 g |
| cappuccino (oat milk) | 240 g | `Oat Milk` → 120 g |
| toast with butter (white) | 45 g | `Bread (White Sliced)` → 30 g · `Butter` → 10 g |
| toast without butter (white) | 30 g | `Bread (White Sliced)` → 30 g |
| toast with butter (wholemeal) | 50 g | `Bread (Wholemeal)` → 36 g · `Butter` → 10 g |
| mashed potato | 200 g | `Potatoes (Boiled)` → 180 g · `Butter` → 10 g · `Milk (Whole)` → 20 g |
| scrambled eggs (2 eggs, butter) | 130 g | `Eggs, Whole (Raw)` → 100 g · `Butter` → 10 g · `Milk (Whole)` → 20 g |
| overnight oats | 300 g | `Oats (Raw)` → 50 g · `Milk (Whole)` → 150 g · `Greek Yogurt (Plain)` → 50 g |
| beans on toast | 260 g | `Baked Beans (Canned)` → 200 g · `Bread (White Sliced)` → 60 g |
| greek yoghurt with honey | 170 g | `Greek Yogurt (Plain)` → 150 g · `Honey` → 15 g |
| cereal with milk | 270 g | `Milk (Whole)` → 200 g *(cereal omitted — highly variable, no single micro profile)* |

**Note on foods without a composite entry:**  
`Tuna Mayo Sandwich`, `Chicken Wrap`, `PB&J Sandwich`, and `Protein Shake` variants are in the Quick-Add list but **not** in `COMPOSITE_FOODS`. Entries with these names fall through to Step 3 of the resolution chain (manual name fallback against `ingredients.json`) and will only get micros if an exact-name match exists there.

## 14. Supplement Tracker

### 14.1 User flow
1. User adds supplements to their "shelf" via the Add Supplement dialog (from catalog or as a custom entry)
2. Optionally groups supplements into stacks (see `/stacks` page)
3. Optionally enables a daily reminder time per supplement
4. Each day, logs intake (taken/skipped) via `supplement_intakes`
5. Micronutrients from **taken** supplements that have a `catalogId` are added to daily AMQS

### 14.2 AMQS micro integration

Only supplements with a `catalogId` (i.e. linked to the `supplement_catalog` table) contribute micronutrients. Custom supplements without a catalog link contribute zero micros.

`server/lib/micros.ts` aggregates supplement micros alongside food micros before AMQS scoring:
```
for each intake on the date where taken === true:
  catalog = supplement_catalog[supplement.catalogId]
  for each nutrient in catalog.microsPerUnit:
    totalMicros[nutrient] += supplement.doseAmount × catalog.microsPerUnit[nutrient]
```

This merged total (food micros + supplement micros) is what feeds `GET /api/me/amqs/micros/:date`.

**UI signal:** On the supplement shelf list, any supplement with a `catalogId` shows a `"AMQS tracked"` badge (default variant) and the sub-line: *"Contributing to your AMQS score"*.

### 14.3 Disclaimer gate for reminders
Before a supplement reminder can be enabled, the user must accept a disclaimer. This is checked via `GET /api/me/disclaimer/supplement_reminders` and accepted via `POST /api/me/disclaimer/supplement_reminders`. The disclaimer type string is `"supplement_reminders"`. The state is stored in `userDisclaimerAcceptance`.

### 14.4 Supplement form — field options

**Form options (physical form of the supplement):**
```
"pill" | "capsule" | "powder" | "liquid" | "tablet" | "softgel" | "gummy" | "other"
```

**Dose units:**
```
"mcg" | "mg" | "g" | "IU" | "ml" | "serving" | "CFU"
```

**Reminder time default:** `"08:00"` (HH:MM string, input type="time")

### 14.5 Add Supplement dialog — complete field spec

Opened by tapping the "Add Supplement" button (`data-testid="button-add-supplement"`).

Fields are **uncontrolled local state** — not react-hook-form. Form is submitted via `onSubmit` handler.

**Field 1 — Catalog selector** (`data-testid="select-catalog"`)
- Label: "Select from Catalog (optional)"
- Component: shadcn `Select`
- First option: `value="custom"` → "Custom Supplement"
- Remaining options: one `SelectItem` per catalog entry (`value=item.id.toString()`, label=`item.name`)
- **On catalog item selected:**
  - Sets `catalogId` state
  - Auto-fills `name` with `item.name`
  - Auto-fills `doseUnit` with `item.defaultUnit`
- **On "custom" selected:** clears `catalogId` and `doseUnit`
- **Catalog hint** (shown only when a catalog item is selected):
  - `bg-secondary/50 p-2 rounded` with `Info` icon
  - Text: `item.notes` if present, otherwise `"This supplement's micronutrients will be tracked for AMQS."`

**Field 2 — Name** (`data-testid="input-supplement-name"`)
- Label: "Supplement Name *"
- Required — submit is blocked if empty
- Placeholder: `"e.g., Vitamin D3"`

**Field 3 + 4 — Dose (2-column grid)**
- Left: Dose Amount (`data-testid="input-dose-amount"`) — `type="number"`, `step="any"`, placeholder `"e.g., 25"`
- Right: Dose Unit (`data-testid="select-dose-unit"`) — shadcn Select, options from `DOSE_UNITS`

**Field 5 — Brand** (`data-testid="input-supplement-brand"`)
- Label: "Brand (optional)"
- Placeholder: `"e.g., Nature Made"`

**Field 6 — Form** (`data-testid="select-supplement-form"`)
- Label: "Form (optional)"
- shadcn Select, options from `FORM_OPTIONS`, all capitalized

**Field 7 — Notes** (`data-testid="input-supplement-notes"`)
- Label: "Notes (optional)"
- shadcn `Textarea`, `resize-none`
- Placeholder: `"Any personal notes..."`

**Field 8 — Daily Reminder toggle** (`data-testid="toggle-reminder-enabled"`)
- Custom toggle switch — NOT a shadcn Switch
- `role="switch"`, `aria-checked={reminderEnabled}`
- Style when off: `bg-secondary`; style when on: `bg-primary`
- Thumb: `h-3.5 w-3.5` white circle, `translate-x-1` (off) → `translate-x-4` (on)
- When toggled on → shows a time input (`data-testid="input-reminder-time"`)
  - `type="time"`, default `"08:00"`
  - Only sent to server when `reminderEnabled === true`

**Submit button** (`data-testid="button-save-supplement"`)
- Label: "Add Supplement" / "Adding..." (pending)
- Disabled when `isPending` or name is empty

**POST body sent to `/api/supplements`:**
```typescript
{
  name:            string          // trimmed, required
  brand?:          string          // trimmed, omitted if empty
  form?:           string          // omitted if empty
  notes?:          string          // trimmed, omitted if empty
  catalogId?:      number          // omitted if custom (no catalogId)
  doseAmount?:     number          // parseFloat, omitted if empty
  doseUnit?:       string          // omitted if empty
  reminderEnabled: boolean
  reminderTime?:   string          // HH:MM, only if reminderEnabled === true
}
```

**On success:** invalidates `["/api/me/supplements"]`, `["/api/me/stacks/scheduled"]`, `["/api/me/amqs/score"]`, `["/api/me/amqs/score-range"]`. Closes dialog. Toast: "Supplement added".

### 14.6 Edit Supplement dialog

Opened by tapping the `Pencil` icon on a supplement row (`data-testid="button-edit-supplement-{id}"`). All fields pre-filled from the existing `Supplement` object.

Identical field layout to Add. Key differences:
- Title: "Edit Supplement"
- Submit button: "Save Changes" / "Saving..."
- Calls `PATCH /api/supplements/{id}`
- Catalog selector: when switching to "custom", does NOT clear the existing `doseUnit` (only sets `catalogId = null`)
- `doseAmount` sent as `null` (not omitted) when cleared; `doseUnit` sent as `null` when cleared; `reminderTime` sent as `null` when reminder disabled

**PATCH body:**
```typescript
{
  name?:            string
  brand?:           string
  form?:            string
  notes?:           string
  catalogId?:       number | null
  doseAmount?:      number | null
  doseUnit?:        string | null
  reminderEnabled?: boolean
  reminderTime?:    string | null
}
```

**On success:** invalidates same 4 query keys as Add. Closes dialog. Toast: "Supplement updated".

### 14.7 Delete supplement

Tapping the `Trash2` icon (`data-testid="button-delete-supplement-{id}"`) immediately fires `DELETE /api/supplements/{id}` — no confirmation dialog. On success: invalidates same 4 query keys. Toast: "Supplement deleted".

### 14.8 Supplement shelf list item — exact row layout

Each `motion.div` item in the `AnimatePresence` list:
```
animation: initial { opacity:0, y:10 } → animate { opacity:1, y:0 }
exit: { opacity:0, x:-20 }
transition: { duration: 0.2 }
className: "flex items-center justify-between p-4 rounded-lg border bg-secondary/30 group"
data-testid: "supplement-item-{supp.id}"
```

Left column (flex-1):
```
Row 1 (flex, items-center, gap-2, flex-wrap):
  <p className="font-medium">{supp.name}</p>
  IF doseAmount && doseUnit:
    <Badge variant="outline" className="text-[10px]">{doseAmount} {doseUnit}</Badge>
  IF form:
    <Badge variant="secondary" className="text-[10px] capitalize">{form}</Badge>
  IF catalogId:
    <Badge variant="default" className="text-[10px]">AMQS tracked</Badge>

Row 2 (conditional, shown when catalogId is set):
  <p className="text-xs text-muted-foreground/60 mt-0.5">Contributing to your AMQS score</p>

Row 3 (conditional, shown when reminderEnabled && reminderTime):
  <p className="text-xs text-primary/70 mt-0.5">⏰ Daily reminder at {reminderTime}</p>

Row 4 (brand + notes):
  IF brand: <span>{brand}</span>
  IF notes: <span className="block text-xs mt-1 italic">{notes}</span>
```

Right column (action buttons):
```
Pencil button: size="icon" variant="ghost"
  className includes "opacity-100 sm:opacity-0 group-hover:opacity-100 transition-opacity"
  data-testid="button-edit-supplement-{supp.id}"

Trash2 button: size="icon" variant="ghost"
  className includes "text-destructive hover:text-destructive"
  data-testid="button-delete-supplement-{supp.id}"
```

### 14.9 Supplement catalog (`GET /api/supplement-catalog`)

Returns all `SupplementCatalogItem[]`. Fetched with `staleTime: 5 * 60 * 1000` (5 min) and `retry: 2`.

Each catalog item has:
```typescript
{
  id:           number
  name:         string
  defaultUnit:  string       // e.g. "mg", "mcg", "IU"
  notes:        string | null
  microsPerUnit: Record<string, number>  // keyed by MICRO_KEYS
}
```

When a catalog item is selected in the Add/Edit form:
1. `name` is auto-populated from `item.name`
2. `doseUnit` is auto-populated from `item.defaultUnit`
3. A hint box appears **immediately below the catalog selector**:
   - Style: `flex items-start gap-2 text-xs text-muted-foreground bg-secondary/50 p-2 rounded`
   - `Info` icon (lucide, `h-3 w-3 mt-0.5 flex-shrink-0`)
   - Text: `item.notes` if the catalog item has notes, otherwise the fallback string `"This supplement's micronutrients will be tracked for AMQS."`
4. On save, `catalogId` is stored → enables `microsPerUnit × doseAmount` micro aggregation server-side

The hint is **only shown when a catalog item is actively selected** (not when "Custom Supplement" is selected or no selection has been made).

> **Catalog content is fully API-driven.** Call `GET /api/supplement-catalog` to get the live list — names, `defaultUnit`, `notes`, and `microsPerUnit` are all returned. No hard-coding needed.

> **Fallback hint** (when `item.notes` is null): `"This supplement's micronutrients will be tracked for AMQS."`

Note: some catalog items have a non-empty `microsPerUnit` (e.g. Vitamin D3, Zinc, Omega-3) while others have an empty `{}` (e.g. Creatine, Vitamin K2). Both show the "AMQS tracked" badge on the shelf because they have a `catalogId`, but only items with non-empty `microsPerUnit` actually contribute to the AMQS score.

If catalog fails to load, a destructive card error is shown at the top of the page (but the form still works — user can add a custom supplement without catalog).

---

## 15. Authentication System

### 15.1 Session auth
- `express-session` + `connect-pg-simple` (sessions stored in PostgreSQL)
- `SESSION_SECRET` env var
- Session cookie: httpOnly, sameSite: 'lax', secure in production

### 15.2 Local strategy (Passport.js)
- Username or email login
- Password hashed with **Argon2** (not bcrypt)
- Email verification required before login (Resend sends verification email)
- Forgot password → time-limited reset link via Resend

### 15.3 Google OAuth 2.0
- `GOOGLE_CLIENT_ID` + `GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET` env vars
- `/auth/google` → Google consent → `/auth/google/callback`
- Creates or links `usersAuth` record on first login

### 15.4 Invite-only beta
- Beta cap controlled by `BETA_USER_LIMIT` env var (currently 200)
- Active user count from `users_auth` table
- New signups require an invite token OR the cap must not be reached
- Invite tokens stored hashed in `invites` table

### 15.5 Username rules
- 3–20 characters, alphanumeric + underscore + hyphen
- Cannot be a reserved word (list in `shared/username-validation.ts`)
- Rate-limited changes: max 2 per 30 days (tracked in `username_changes`)

### 15.6 Special account: `onboardtester`
After `POST /api/user/me/onboard` completes for username `onboardtester`, a 90-second `setTimeout` resets all profile fields to null — keeping this account perpetually ready for fresh onboarding demos in production.

---

## 16. Full API Endpoint Reference

All endpoints require an authenticated session unless noted as **Public**.  
All responses are JSON. Error format: `{ message: string }`.  
All `/api` routes have `Cache-Control: no-store` globally applied.

---

### 16.1 Authentication (`/api/auth/*`)

Mounted via `app.use("/api/auth", authRoutes)`. Rate-limited: 10 req / 15 min for login/register/reset.

| Method | Path | Auth | Request body | Validation | Response |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| POST | `/api/auth/register` | Public | `{ email, username, password, inviteToken, source? }` | `insertAuthUserSchema` + invite token check + beta cap | 201 `{ user: { id, email, username, emailVerified: false } }` |
| POST | `/api/auth/login` | Public | `{ identifier, password }` | identifier min 1, password min 1 | `{ user: { id, email, username, emailVerified } }` |
| POST | `/api/auth/logout` | Yes | Empty | — | `{ ok: true }` + clears `connect.sid` cookie |
| GET  | `/api/auth/me` | Yes | — | — | `{ user: { id, email, username, emailVerified } }` |
| POST | `/api/auth/resend-verification` | Yes | Empty | — | `{ message }` (3 req / 15 min) |
| GET  | `/api/auth/verify-email?token=` | Public | Query: `token` | Token from DB | Redirect to `/verify-email?success=1` or `?error=...` |
| POST | `/api/auth/forgot-password` | Public | `{ email }` | Email format | `{ message }` — same response always (no user enumeration); 5 req / 15 min |
| POST | `/api/auth/reset-password` | Public | `{ token, password }` | password: min 8 chars, ≥1 letter, ≥1 digit | `{ message }` |
| POST | `/api/auth/change-email` | Yes | `{ newEmail }` | Email format | `{ message }` + sends verification email |
| GET  | `/api/auth/username-available?username=` | Public | Query: `username` | `validateUsername()` | `{ available: boolean, error?: string }` |
| PATCH | `/api/auth/username` | Yes | `{ username }` | `validateUsername()` + 3 per 24h rate limit | `{ message, newUsername }` or 429 `{ error, code: "RATE_LIMITED", nextAllowedAt }` |
| GET  | `/api/auth/notifications/vapid-public-key` | Public | — | — | `{ publicKey }` |
| GET  | `/api/auth/notifications/status` | Public | — | — | `{ enabled: boolean }` |
| POST | `/api/auth/notifications/subscribe` | Yes | `{ endpoint: URL, keys: { p256dh, auth } }` | Zod URL + key presence | `{ message }` |
| POST | `/api/auth/notifications/unsubscribe` | Yes | `{ endpoint }` | endpoint presence | `{ message }` |
| POST | `/api/auth/notifications/test` | Yes | Empty | — | `{ message, sent, failed }` |
| GET  | `/auth/google` | Public | — | — | Redirect to Google consent (no `/api` prefix) |
| GET  | `/auth/google/callback` | Public | — | — | Redirect to `/dashboard` or `/?error=google_auth_failed` (no `/api` prefix) |

**`insertAuthUserSchema` fields:**
- `email`: valid email, lowercased
- `username`: 3–20 chars, alphanumeric/underscore/hyphen, normalised to lowercase, not reserved
- `password`: min 8 chars, ≥1 letter, ≥1 digit

**Username rate limit:** max 3 changes per 24 hours per user. Returns HTTP 429 with `{ error, code: "RATE_LIMITED", nextAllowedAt: ISO string }`.

---

### 16.2 Invites (`/api/invites/*`)

Mounted via `app.use("/api/invites", inviteRoutes)`. Rate-limited: 5 req / hr.

| Method | Path | Auth | Request body | Response |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| POST | `/api/invites/request` | Public | `{ email, source? }` | `{ message }` — sends invite code email. 403 if beta full (added to waitlist). |
| GET  | `/api/invites/validate?token=` | Public | Query: `token` | `{ valid: boolean, email?, error? }` |

Invite codes: 10-char uppercase alphanumeric, valid 7 days, max 1 use, stored as SHA-256 hash.

### 16.3 Feedback (`/api/feedback/*`)

Rate-limited: 5 submissions / hr per user.

| Method | Path | Auth | Request body | Response |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| POST | `/api/feedback/upload-url` | Yes | `{ name, size, contentType }` | `{ uploadURL, objectPath, metadata }` — contentType must be `image/png`, `image/jpeg`, or `image/webp`; size < 5 MB |
| POST | `/api/feedback` | Yes | `{ category, message, route?, userAgent?, viewport?, appVersion?, attachments?: [{url, filename, mimeType, size}] }` | 201 `{ ...feedback, attachments: [] }` — attachment `url` must start with `/objects/uploads/`, max 3 |
| GET  | `/api/feedback/mine` | Yes | — | Last 10 feedback items for the authenticated user |
